<div id="review_275413524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/275413524" />
    <a title="Mimi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/981011-mimi"><img alt="Mimi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287101719p2/981011.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/275413524?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mimi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mimi" href="/user/show/981011-mimi">Mimi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/981011-mimi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer275413524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17753199755946439547">I give the rating of two stars in its truest sense of "it's okay." This was a difficult novel to rate. I thought the writing was really good, and it was funny. But the main characters were all so incredible. They were all wealthy (or at least not poor), they all were really smart/got good grades, they were all really talented in different ways, they were all very attractive, etc. And I guess it is quite possible that three people like them would all be friends, so I don't know why I'm complainin</span>
  <span id="freeText17753199755946439547" style="display:none">I give the rating of two stars in its truest sense of "it's okay." This was a difficult novel to rate. I thought the writing was really good, and it was funny. But the main characters were all so incredible. They were all wealthy (or at least not poor), they all were really smart/got good grades, they were all really talented in different ways, they were all very attractive, etc. And I guess it is quite possible that three people like them would all be friends, so I don't know why I'm complaining about that. But I mean, both main male characters lettered in three sports, got straight As, were really nice to people, and did either comedy or musical theater. Are there that many guys like that running around high school? Jocks, nerds, and thespians all rolled into one?<br /><br />And then you find out that one of them is gay, and the only reaction his best friend/brother has is "oh, I'm so glad you finally figured out that you were gay." It just seems like if I were a boy who had a best friend who was more like a brother, who I had a bed for in my bedroom and a bed of my own in his bedroom at his house that finding out he is gay would change the dynamic of the relationship a bit, at least a little. But no one seemed to mind. His best friends, his parents, etc. It was all taken in stride. The only mention of gay not being completely mainstream and normal was one sentence where the non-gay friend said that sometimes he was called a "fag" by people who assumed he was gay because they were such good friends. But he said he didn't mind that misconception, because girls seemed to take that as a challenge and chase him all the more. (I don't know if "fag" is a swear word or just a rude word, so I didn't know whether to type it out or asterisk it, but know that it is a not a word I ever say.) And I am not trying to imply that it should be a problem or come between them; I simply thought it might be something that would require more of a discussion between them.<br /><br />The story line between Ale and Anthony is really sweet. And I loved the story line involving Hucky. He's just amazing. It is so sad that some parents with disabled children really can do things like that. I loved the sweet miracle of <i>Mary Poppins</i> and wish we could all keep more of the childhood magic alive in our lives. American Sign Language keeps popping up everywhere in my life (books, shows, seeing people sign when I'm out). I'm starting to wonder if I should try learning it. But I don't actually know any deaf people.<br /><br />I found the parts very interesting that talked about how TC dealt with losing his mother when he was only six. And I really liked the close relationship that he shared with his father. Actually, all of these teenagers had good relationships with their parents. Their parents were all pretty involved in their lives, which seems to be rare in media portrayals of teenagers. Granted, Ale did hide from her parents that she was taking singing and dancing classes instead of French classes, but she did eventually come clean. And that is much smaller than some secrets teens have from their parents!<br /><br />I really liked that these were high schoolers in a contemporary novel, but their relationships never went further than kissing.<br /><br />There were a few comments that were anatomical in nature.<br /><br />And I really think that it is not fair that boys don't get to have shower curtains in their locker rooms at schools. Girls get them. Boys should have them, too.<br /><br />I picked up the book, because it was a YA book written by a male with two male protagonists, and I really was curious to see what they would be thinking and how it would turn out. And then I kept reading it, because I was interested what their view of the gay issue would be. <br /><br />There was one completely unnecessary "F" word. And not even spoken. Just a character sketch in Anthony's journal about Bucky F. Dent. (But the F was not abbreviated.) Anthony is very much a Boston Red Sox fan.<br /><br />I did like this quote. "Did you ever take modern dance . . .? Did you know that your body can say more with eight bars of music than you could possibly write in a fifteen-page essay?"<br /><br />Augie's feminist journalist mother brought out some points regarding musicals that I had never thought of before. <br /><br />Most of the baseball references and music references were over my head.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17753199755946439547" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_40035638" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40035638" />
    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1676535-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499022950p2/1676535.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40035638?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/1676535-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40035638" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5464898965972777538">My Most Excellent Year tells the story of three students- now seniors-most excellent year (their freshman year) and how their lives all changed for the better. First, there’s T.C.( Anthony), who’s obsessed with all things related to baseball, his best friend Augie, and Alejeandra, the girl he’s in love with, but who doesn’t return his feelings. Augie loves all things that have to do with Broadway and his best friend T.C. Also, everyone knows Augie‘s gay, but he just hasn‘t realized his true feel</span>
  <span id="freeText5464898965972777538" style="display:none">My Most Excellent Year tells the story of three students- now seniors-most excellent year (their freshman year) and how their lives all changed for the better. First, there’s T.C.( Anthony), who’s obsessed with all things related to baseball, his best friend Augie, and Alejeandra, the girl he’s in love with, but who doesn’t return his feelings. Augie loves all things that have to do with Broadway and his best friend T.C. Also, everyone knows Augie‘s gay, but he just hasn‘t realized his true feelings yet. Lastly, there is Alejeandra. Alejeandra grew up in a very political and fundamental family. Her father is a rich diplomat. Though, Alejeandra is expected to grow up to be just like her parents and her brother her true love is dancing and singing which is unacceptable to her family. As, she pursues this passion in life she begins to become friends with Augie and T.C. and just may fall in love with the T.C.<br /><br />My Most Excellent Year was a truly hysterical and cute read that had me turning the pages nonstop. Steve Kluger told this story in diary entrees, instant message conversations, and letters. I’ve read this type of writing before, but have never enjoyed it as much as in this novel. It let me get to know the characters, probably better than it being told in first or third person, and it kept the story interesting most of the time. At the beginning his writing could feel a bit so- so , but as the story continued, and as the characters began to get more developed, it picked up and started to get pretty funny. Especially during Augie’s parts. Also, I enjoyed seeing how each character began to grow in one way or another throughout the novel. At the end, I was sad to see it come to a close, but knew that it was just the right time to conclude it. Overall, this story was a cute coming of age novel that I recommend to all age groups. Be aware, though, that the beginning was a tad boring. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5464898965972777538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniel" href="/user/show/29777818-daniel">Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25127550-my-most-excellent-year">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29777818-daniel?shelf=epistolary">epistolary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1275976415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10773025047965792218">So... It's epistolary which is always fun. Emails, IMs, diary entries. No direct narration.<br/><br/>I read it in about three sittings in a single day, stayed up till 2 am finishing it. Mostly because the characters are adorable than any real suspense. The book seems pretty low on conflict to me, though I haven't read a ton of YA stuff to compare it to. It's basically two 14 year olds one straight, one gay, finding their first loves, and the biggest worries are does she/he like me. The parents are pretty </span>
  <span id="freeText10773025047965792218" style="display:none">So... It's epistolary which is always fun. Emails, IMs, diary entries. No direct narration.<br /><br />I read it in about three sittings in a single day, stayed up till 2 am finishing it. Mostly because the characters are adorable than any real suspense. The book seems pretty low on conflict to me, though I haven't read a ton of YA stuff to compare it to. It's basically two 14 year olds one straight, one gay, finding their first loves, and the biggest worries are does she/he like me. The parents are pretty much ideal understanding accepting types and not a source of conflict. I guess Alejandra's do provide a tiny bit of resistance but, meh. It reminded me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a> a bit, but with less (virtually no) gloomy brooding. <br /><br />Structurally the book felt rather haphazard to me. With the lack of conflict and the rather easy way the characters got to the first stages of their relationships, it seemed like the book could have just stopped about 1/3 of the way in and been a sweet, cute little novella, but then Kluger throws a six year old deaf boy who's obsessed with Mary Poppins into their lives and he gives the book a reason to keep going. <br /><br />I liked this <i>much</i> better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/239092.Almost_Like_Being_in_Love" title="Almost Like Being in Love by Steve Kluger" rel="nofollow noopener">Almost Like Being in Love</a> which is the only other thing I've read by the author. It doesn't have any of the things that annoyed me about that book, but is told in much the same way.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10773025047965792218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_61270737" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61270737" />
    <a title="Hallie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie"><img alt="Hallie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1244842998p2/1145657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/61270737?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hallie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hallie" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie">Hallie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=ya">ya</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61270737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8841442618890352441">My feelings are a bit mixed (yes, again!), as there were a lot of things I loved about this book: T.C.'s beautifully described memories of his mother, and the ways he dealt with them, and how he and Augie came to be 'brothers' were especially good - funny and very real. And of course the whole heart-string tugging storyline of Hucky tugged very effectively, even if it was easy to see how that one would end up from the beginning. I also <i>liked</i> the fact that everyone around Augie was so far beyond </span>
  <span id="freeText8841442618890352441" style="display:none">My feelings are a bit mixed (yes, again!), as there were a lot of things I loved about this book: T.C.'s beautifully described memories of his mother, and the ways he dealt with them, and how he and Augie came to be 'brothers' were especially good - funny and very real. And of course the whole heart-string tugging storyline of Hucky tugged very effectively, even if it was easy to see how that one would end up from the beginning. I also <i>liked</i> the fact that everyone around Augie was so far beyond just 'okay' with his being gay that it became funny, but also had some hesitation about that. His sections were almost unreadably sappy at times, as he went on *endlessly* over his swooning love and every single high and low of the whole relationship. And a lot of the humour of everyone's cheerful acceptance of his being gay came from his hitting every single stereotype of a <i>camp</i> gay teen ever encountered. Which left me a bit distressed. But as I said, much good, and mostly the sappy bits were countered by T.C.'s puncturing of them and Alé's sharpness and the families' coolness.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8841442618890352441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_26896798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26896798" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/723940-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1198945774p2/723940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26896798?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/723940-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who need entertaining</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/723940-heather?shelf=ya-fiction">ya-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/723940-heather?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26896798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13969354372711992517">WHY ISN'T EVERYONE READING THIS BOOK? It was great! First of all, there are three characters who are well written, well developed, and not too angsty. They are mostly happy, with adults involved in their lives (adults who think their kids are cool and smart), and it is an INTERESTING storyline, complete with Julie Andrews. <br/>On a side note, I am interested in the people who qualify this as a "LGBT" YA book, instead of just a great YA book. I have read goodreads readers who said it was unrealistic.</span>
  <span id="freeText13969354372711992517" style="display:none">WHY ISN'T EVERYONE READING THIS BOOK? It was great! First of all, there are three characters who are well written, well developed, and not too angsty. They are mostly happy, with adults involved in their lives (adults who think their kids are cool and smart), and it is an INTERESTING storyline, complete with Julie Andrews. <br />On a side note, I am interested in the people who qualify this as a "LGBT" YA book, instead of just a great YA book. I have read goodreads readers who said it was unrealistic. Maybe that's true. Maybe it's not. Maybe the coming generation will be the ones to whom race and sexuality is not a big deal. Hmm. I would be interested in your opinions. <br />And also, I loved this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2393976574420655490">Totally cute! First loves, musicals, and a little deaf orphan waiting for Mary Poppins to adopt him! Adorable! Also worth mentioning, the father and son who can't just make a presentation about a monument in DC, but instead have to make a scale model of the National Mall, political conversations about the interned Japanese in WWII, and a variety of races and sexual orientations happily existing in a book without shouting LOOK AT US! WE'RE DIFFERENT! <br/><br/>The negative: Red Sox. Though I did like the i</span>
  <span id="freeText2393976574420655490" style="display:none">Totally cute! First loves, musicals, and a little deaf orphan waiting for Mary Poppins to adopt him! Adorable! Also worth mentioning, the father and son who can't just make a presentation about a monument in DC, but instead have to make a scale model of the National Mall, political conversations about the interned Japanese in WWII, and a variety of races and sexual orientations happily existing in a book without shouting LOOK AT US! WE'RE DIFFERENT! <br /><br />The negative: Red Sox. Though I did like the insinuations that the CIA are head hunting for them. :)</span>

<div id="review_598003521" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/598003521" />
    <a title="Diana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/857820-diana"><img alt="Diana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1443398848p2/857820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/598003521?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diana" href="/user/show/857820-diana">Diana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer598003521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16728529284921082056">This is one of the cutest books I've read. It's written in unconventional formats of letters, emails and IM's so it goes by quick. The characters are funny and charming, and I found myself smiling the whole time I was reading this with the occasional laugh. The writing is sincere and Kluger does an excellent job making the reader feel like they're part of the story. After I read the last page, I wanted to give the main characters a hug.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2875472653" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2875472653" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3142267-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2875472653?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/3142267-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2875472653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8026669229335754352">A charming YA book with quirky, smart teenage characters; gay and straight romantic story lines; a variety of writing mediums; heartwarming messages about love and family and community; AND a Julie Andrews cameo! Oh, and baseball for the more sports-minded reader. I'm not sure if the book would appeal to the average contemporary teenager, but this middle-aged, life-long musical theater fan found it delightful. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g5rJKbRx4Gh4qZThl/tw7420gPSHrGlhzUjlHrC4K5fWezntjBLUJal16+Pvo6CZp7OmUAwaMjRHtHUrkYKnKA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YGNqKC45lkc4/GeA6VF3wDERTz5wQjpBM/zG6KXV5Wo1gprsFlqiCukgGIKRCae2GxZpmvv0YRS5AFbdhO9p1Q==')})
  }
//]]>

social rebels severing their attachments to American culture to remake themselves in their own image. 1960s comic book creators, anticipating Fiedler, began to morph American superheroes from icons of nationalism and white masculinity into actual mutant outcasts, defined by their genetic difference from ordinary humanity. These powerful misfits and &quot;freaks&quot; soon came to embody the social and political aspirations of America\'s most marginalized groups, including women, racial and sexual minorities, and the working classes.\n\n\n\nIn The New Mutants, Ramzi Fawaz draws upon queer theory to tell the story of these monstrous fantasy figures and how they grapple with radical politics from Civil Rights and The New Left to Women\'s and Gay Liberation Movements. Through a series of comic book case studies - including The Justice League of America, The Fantastic Four, The X-Men, and The New Mutants -alongside late 20th century fan writing, cultural criticism, and political documents, Fawaz reveals how the American superhero modeled new forms of social belonging that counterculture youth would embrace in the 1960s and after.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/65944.Steve_Kluger">About Steve Kluger</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/65944.Steve_Kluger"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1460902377p3/65944.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/65944.Steve_Kluger">Steve Kluger
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer90206603815449463">Steve Kluger is an author and playwright, born in Baltimore, Maryland, in 1952, who grew up with only two heroes: Tom Seaver and Ethel Merman. Few were able to grasp the concept. A veteran of "Casablanca" and a graduate of "The Graduate," he has written extensively on subjects as far ranging as World War II, rock and roll, and the Titanic, and as close to the heart as baseball and the Boston Red S</span>
  <span id="freeText90206603815449463" style="display:none">Steve Kluger is an author and playwright, born in Baltimore, Maryland, in 1952, who grew up with only two heroes: Tom Seaver and Ethel Merman. Few were able to grasp the concept. A veteran of "Casablanca" and a graduate of "The Graduate," he has written extensively on subjects as far ranging as World War II, rock and roll, and the Titanic, and as close to the heart as baseball and the Boston Red Sox (which frequently have nothing to do with one another). Doubtless due to the fact that he's a card-carrying Baby Boomer whose entire existence was shaped by the lyrics to "Abbey Road," "Workingman's Dead," and "Annie Get Your Gun" (his first spoken words, in fact, were actually stolen from "The Pajama Game"), he's also forged a somewhat singular path as a civil rights advocate, campaigning for a "Save Fenway Park" initiative (which qualifies as a civil right if you're a Red Sox fan), counseling gay teenagers, and--on behalf of Japanese American internment redress--lobbying the Department of the Interior to restore the baseball diamond at he Manzanar National Historic Site. Meanwhile, he donates half of his spare time to organizations such as Lambda Legal Defense, the Gay, Lesbian, Straight Education Network (GLSEN), and Models of Pride, and gives the rest of it to his nieces and nephews--the nine kids who own his heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="90206603815449463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
